<span class="italic"><a title="Link to journal home page" href="https://doi.org/10.1039/2040-3372/2009">Nanoscale</a></span>, 2020, <strong>12</strong>, 20337-20346</div><h1 id="sect202"><span class="title_heading">The electrochemical storage mechanism of an In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode for high-performance Li-ion and Na-ion batteries<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></span></h1><p class="header_text">

      <br><a id="affa"><sup><span class="sup_ref italic">a</span></sup></a><span class="italic">National Base for International Science &amp; Technology Cooperation, National Local Joint Engineering Laboratory for Key Materials of New Energy Storage Battery, Hunan Province Key Laboratory of Electrochemical Energy Storage and Conversion, School of Chemistry, Xiangtan University, Xiangtan 411105, China.     </p><div id="art-admin"><span class="italic bold">Received 
      27th June 2020
    </span><span class="bold italic">, Accepted 7th September 2020</span></div><p class="bold italic">First published on 17th September 2020</p><hr><div class="abstract"><h2>Abstract</h2><p>There are only a handful of reports on indium sulfide (In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>) in the electrochemical energy storage field without a clear electrochemical reaction mechanism. In this work, a simple electrospinning method has been used to synthesize In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers for the first time. In lithium-ion batteries (LIBs), the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode can not only deliver a high initial reversible specific capacity of 696.4 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, but also shows ultra-long cycle life with a capacity retention of 80.5% after 600 cycles at 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. In sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers electrode can exhibit a high initial reversible specific capacity (393.7 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>) and excellent cycling performance with a high capacity retention of 97.3% after 300 cycles at 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The excellent electrochemical properties mainly benefited from In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> being encapsulated by a carbon matrix, which buffers the volume expansion and significantly improves the conductivity of the composite. Furthermore, the structural evolution of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> during the first lithiation/delithiation and sodiation/desodiation processes has been illustrated by <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD. The results confirm that the reaction mechanism of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in both LIBs and SIBs can be summarized as conversion reactions and alloying reactions, which provide theoretical support for the development of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in the field of electrochemistry.</p></div><hr>
    
      
      <h2 id="sect307"><span class="a_heading">1. Introduction</span></h2>
      <span>As a mature energy storage device, lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been extensively used in various electronic devices, such as computers, smart phones and electric vehicles.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit1"><sup><span class="sup_ref">13</span></sup></a> However, the pursuit of higher capacity will never stop and the limited lithium source inhibits their large-scale applications.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit4"><sup><span class="sup_ref">4</span></sup></a> Sodium ion batteries (SIBs), as an energy storage device with an electrochemical mechanism similar to LIBs, have been brought into the spotlight on account of the abundant sodium resources on the Earth.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit5"><sup><span class="sup_ref">59</span></sup></a> However, many anode materials used for LIBs are not appropriate for SIBs. For instance, the traditional graphite material reported in previous studies has a low specific capacity of below 35 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> in SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit10"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1012</span></sup></a> Although some reported carbon-based materials, like hard carbon and expanded graphite, exhibit enhanced sodium storage capacity, their capacity is still less than 300 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at relatively low current densities.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit13"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1315</span></sup></a> Hence, it is urgent to develop high-performance anode materials that can be applied in both LIBs and SIBs.</span>
      <p class="otherpara">Transition metal sulfides (such as Sb<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, SnS, MoS<small><sub>2</sub></small>, and SnS<small><sub>2</sub></small>), which have high theoretical specific capacity in both LIBs and SIBs based on the conversion reaction and the alloying reaction, have attracted extensive attention from researchers.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit16"><sup><span class="sup_ref">1622</span></sup></a> However, while providing high capacity, the alloying reactions induce large volume expansion,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit23"><sup><span class="sup_ref">23,24</span></sup></a> which causes separation of the active materials from the metal current collector, leading to a continuous capacity fade. Except for the above-listed transition metal sulfides, recent research indicates that indium sulfide (In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>) can also deliver high capacity in both LIBs and SIBs. For instance, the RGOIn<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> composites reported by Ye (<span class="italic">et al</span>.) maintain a high specific capacity of 604 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 200 cycles in LIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25</span></sup></a> Sun's group prepared In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>-graphene composites by the method of hydrothermal calcination and achieved a maximum sodium storage capacity of 620 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26</span></sup></a> However, the electrochemical properties, especially the cycling performance, urgently need further improvement. In addition, In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> has the characteristics of vacancy defects, which can hold more Li<small><sup>+</sup></small>/Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27,28</span></sup></a> Nevertheless, the lithium and sodium storage mechanisms of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> have not been elucidated so far.</p>
      <p class="otherpara">Electrospinning technology is a versatile strategy which can achieve <span class="italic">in situ</span> composites with a carbon matrix for improving the electrochemical performance of active materials. Herein, a novel In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber was synthesized by electrospinning for the first time. The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers have a 1D nanofibrous morphology with a uniform diameter of around 320370 nm. The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers show excellent lithium/sodium storage properties such as high specific capacity, long cycle life, and good rate performance. In addition, <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD was implemented to inquire into the reaction mechanism of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in both LIBs and SIBs. The research results indicate that the capacity of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanofibers in both LIBs and SIBs is provided by the conversion reaction and alloying reaction, and their maximum theoretical specific capacities are 1206 and 658 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively.</p>
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect357"><span class="a_heading">2. Results and discussion</span></h2>
      
        
        <h3 id="sect360"><span class="b_heading">2.1 Synthesis and characterization of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers</span></h3>
        <span>In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers were prepared by a simple method of electrospinning. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig1">Fig. 1</a> reveals the synthesis procedure of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, which can be summarized in the following three steps. Firstly, the precursor solution was electrospun to form a nanofiber membrane. Afterwards, the nanofiber membrane was pre-oxidized in air, which can stabilize the structure of the nanofibers. Finally, the stabilized nanofibers were successively vulcanized and carbonized in a N<small><sub>2</sub></small> atmosphere. In this calcination process, thiourea was decomposed into CS<small><sub>2</sub></small>, acting as the sulfur source of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit29"><sup><span class="sup_ref">29</span></sup></a> More specific details about the experiment can be found in the ESI.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a></span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig1"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f1_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f1.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f1.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 1 </b> <span id="fig1"><span class="graphic_title">Synthesis process of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">The crystallographic structure of the as-prepared In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers was manifested by X-ray diffraction (XRD) analysis and is shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2a</a>. All the identified diffraction peaks agree with tetragonal In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> (JCPDS card no. 25-0390) without an impure phase,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit30"><sup><span class="sup_ref">30,31</span></sup></a> indicating that In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> was successfully synthesized by the electrospinning method. The inset of <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2b</a> shows the crystal structure of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>. There are plenty of vacancies in the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> crystal due to the incomplete coordination of S atoms. These vacancies can provide transport channels for Li<small><sup>+</sup></small>/Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit27"><sup><span class="sup_ref">27,28</span></sup></a> In the Raman scattering spectrum (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2b</a>), there are two peaks at about 1340 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 1590 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> corresponding to the D peak (the disordered structure of carbon) and the G peak (the graphitic structure of carbon), respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit32"><sup><span class="sup_ref">32,33</span></sup></a> The intensity ratio of D to G (<span class="italic">I</span><small><sub>D</sub></small>/<span class="italic">I</span><small><sub>G</sub></small>) is 1.19, indicating the nature of amorphous carbon with partial graphitization. There are some defects in the amorphous carbon structure providing some active sites for the storage of Li<small><sup>+</sup></small>/Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit34"><sup><span class="sup_ref">34</span></sup></a> In addition, in the low Raman shift range, the peaks located at 244.3 (A<small><sub>1g</sub></small>), 307.2 (A<small><sub>1g</sub></small>), 367.3 (A<small><sub>1g</sub></small>), 326.7 (F<small><sub>2g</sub></small>), and 264.7 cm<small><sup>1</sup></small> (E<small><sub>1g</sub></small>) are consistent with the typical Raman modes of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit35"><sup><span class="sup_ref">35</span></sup></a></p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig2"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f2_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f2.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f2.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 2 </b> <span id="fig2"><span class="graphic_title">(a) XRD pattern and (b) Raman spectrum of the as-prepared In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">The electronic valence and composition of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers were detected with X-ray photoelectron spectrometry (XPS) analysis. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3a</a> shows the full spectrum of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, revealing that the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers contain four elements of In, N, C, and S. In the high-resolution In 3d XPS spectrum (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3b</a>), the two peaks located at 444.9 and 452.5 eV correspond to In 3d5/2 and In 3d3/2 of In<small><sup>3+</sup></small> in In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, respectively. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3c</a> shows that the high-resolution S 2p spectrum has two peaks at 163.2 and 162.4 eV, which are consistent with S 2p3/2 and S 2p1/2 of S<small><sup>2</sup></small> in In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, respectively.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit36"><sup><span class="sup_ref">36</span></sup></a> In <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3d</a>, the two peaks at 286.0 eV and 284.6 eV of the C 1s spectrum can be fitted to the CN bonds and CC bonds, respectively. The presence of the CN bonds manifests that N elements from PVP and PAN have been successfully incorporated into the carbon matrix. The doping of nitrogen can provide more electrons for the -conjugated system of carbon, thereby improving the electronic conductivity of the composite.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit37"><sup><span class="sup_ref">37</span></sup></a> The N 1s spectrum shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3e</a> reveals that N mainly exists in the form of pyridinic N (398.0 eV), pyrrolic N (399.7 eV), and graphitic N (400.1 eV), which further implies that nitrogen was successfully doped into the carbon nanofibers (5.6 at% nitrogen content determined with XPS composition analysis). Among them, the defects in the carbon matrix caused by pyridinic N and pyrrolic N can provide some active sites for the intercalation of Li<small><sup>+</sup></small> and Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit38"><sup><span class="sup_ref">3840</span></sup></a></p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig3"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f3_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f3.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f3.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 3 </b> <span id="fig3"><span class="graphic_title">(a) XPS full spectrum, (b) In 3d spectrum, (c) S 2p spectrum, (d) C 1s spectrum, (e) N 1s spectrum of the as-prepared In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, and (f) TG analysis of the as-prepared In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">The carbon content of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers was determined through the thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) and the results are shown in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3f</a>. It can be seen from <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig3">Fig. 3f</a> that there is a slight weight loss below 200 C, which is ascribed to the evaporation of physically adsorbed water and free water.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit41"><sup><span class="sup_ref">41</span></sup></a> The main weight loss of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> occurs between 500 C to 600 C, which can be attributed to the oxidation of carbon and In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in air. Subsequently, the TG curve tends to be flat, and the final total weight loss is 36.6%. XRD characterization of the combustion products (Fig. S1<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) indicates that the final residue was identified as In<small><sub>2</sub></small>O<small><sub>3</sub></small>; therefore, the content of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in the composite can be calculated to be 74.4%.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The morphology of the as-prepared In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers was observed by field emission scanning electron microscopy (FE-SEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM). The FE-SEM image of the precursor fibers in Fig. S2<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> shows that the nanofibers have a smooth fiber surface and uniform fiber diameter of about 350400 nm. After calcination, the FE-SEM images of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers (Fig. S3a and b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) with rough surfaces can be observed at low magnification, and the diameter of the nanofibers is about 320370 nm. Under high magnification (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4a and b</a>), it can be intuitively observed that the surface of the nanofiber is covered with a layer of floc and has been identified as a composite of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles and a thin layer of amorphous carbon using TEM analysis below. The two curves in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4c</a> represent the nitrogen adsorptiondesorption isotherms of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers and the pore size distribution, respectively. The distinct hysteresis loop located at low and middle pressures indicates that there are many micropores and mesopores inside the material, which is consistent with its pore size distribution. The specific surface area and the pore volume were calculated to be 162.5 m<small><sup>2</sup></small> g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 0.098 cm<small><sup>3</sup></small> g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. The large specific surface area and porous structure can buffer the volume expansion caused by the electrochemical reaction; in the meantime, it can also increase the contact area between the electrolyte and the electrode.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit42"><sup><span class="sup_ref">42</span></sup></a></p>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig4"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f4_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f4.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f4.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 4 </b> <span id="fig4"><span class="graphic_title">(a and b) FE-SEM images of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers at different magnifications, (c) N<small><sub>2</sub></small> adsorptiondesorption isotherm and pore size distribution of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, (d) TEM images of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, (e) HR-TEM image and corresponding FFT image (inset) of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, (f) the HAADF image of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, and (gj) EDX elemental mapping images of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">
          <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4d and e</a> show the TEM image and the high-resolution TEM image of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers, respectively. The legible lattice fringes with a space of 6.1  correspond to the (1 0 3) plane of tetragonal In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, which is in agreement with the XRD result. The fast Fourier transform (FFT) image in the inset of <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4e</a> reveals clear diffraction points indicating the high crystallinity of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>. It can be seen from Fig. S4a<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> that there is a layer of floc on the fiber surface, which also confirms the result of the SEM analysis. When the red rectangular frame in Fig. S4a<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> is enlarged, it can be observed that there are some black crystal particles in the floc (as shown by the yellow dashed frame in Fig. S4b<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The high-resolution image (Fig. S4d<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) of the black crystal particles in the red rectangle in Fig. S4c<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> and the interplanar crystal spacing statistical tables (the inset in Fig. S4d<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) are shown in Fig. S4d.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The lattice fringes with a pitch of 3.2  corresponding to the (109) plane of tetragonal In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> can be identified. Therefore, the floc on the fiber surface should be composed of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles and a thin layer of amorphous carbon. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4(gj)</a> display the energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDX) elemental mapping of C, In, S, and, N with the test area corresponding to the high-angle annular dark field (HAADF) image in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4f</a>. It can be seen directly that the four elements C, In, S, and N are uniformly distributed in the nanofibers. However, some light spots can be observed in the elemental mapping of In and S (as shown by the red dashed box in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig4">Fig. 4f, h and i</a>), which correspond to the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> particles in the floc on the fiber surface.</p>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect524"><span class="b_heading">2.2 Lithium storage performance and lithium storage mechanism</span></h3>
        <span>To elucidate the lithium storage mechanism of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, cyclic voltammetry (CV) and <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD have been employed to research the phase transition during the electrochemical reaction. The CV curves in the voltage range from 0.01 to 3.0 V can be seen in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5a</a>. The reduction peak corresponding to the conversion reaction of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> to In and Li<small><sub>2</sub></small>S is located at 0.99 V in the first cathodic scan (<a title="" href="#eqn1">eqn (1)</a>), which can be confirmed by <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD characterization in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5b</a>. When discharged to 0.4 V, a weak diffraction peak appeared at 65.2, which matched the (4 0 0) plane of Li<small><sub>2</sub></small>S. Moreover, the diffraction peaks at 33.0, 36.3, 39.1, 54.5, 63.2, and 67.0 correspond to the (1 0 1), (0 0 2), (1 1 0), (1 1 2), (1 0 3), and (2 1 1) planes of tetragonal In, respectively. The cathodic peaks at 0.68 V in the first scan are related to the irreversible formation of the SEI film, and the cathodic peaks below 0.6 V may be attributable to the InLi alloying reaction (<a title="" href="#eqn2">eqn (2)</a>). In <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5b</a>, two weak diffraction peaks appeared at 32.0 and 34.3 when discharged to 0.01 V, and disappeared when the voltage was charged to 0.4 V, which can be attributed to the (4 2 2) and (5 1 1) planes of cubic In<small><sub>3</sub></small>Li<small><sub>13</sub></small>, respectively. Therefore, the anodic peaks between 0.1 and 0.7 V correspond to the step-by-step dealloying reaction. The broad oxidation peak at 1.05 V in the CV curve (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5a</a>) corresponds to the conversion of In to In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>. However, the peak intensity decreases with an increase of the number of cycles, implying the poor reversibility of the reverse conversion reaction during the charging process. Therefore, In was only partially converted to In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> during the reverse conversion reaction. When the voltage is charged to 1.6 and 3.0 V, a diffraction peak appears at 33.2, which corresponds to the (0 0 12) plane of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig2">Fig. 2a</a>). Moreover, the diffraction peak of In can also be clearly observed in the <span class="italic">ex-situ</span> XRD pattern at cha-3.0 V, which once again confirms that In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> is only partially reversible. The conversion reactions per metal center are accompanied by multiple electron transfers, which makes the conversion from In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> to Li<small><sub>2</sub></small>S and In in the initial lithiation process largely irreversible.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit43"><sup><span class="sup_ref">43</span></sup></a> The low reversibility of the conversion reaction gives rise to the first irreversible capacity loss and a gradual decrease in the capacity during the initial several cycles. It is worth adding that the irreversible formation of the solid electrolyte interphase (SEI) film is also responsible for the first irreversible capacity loss.<table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn1"><span id="eqn1">In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> + 6Li<small><sup>+</sup></small> + 6e<small><sup></sup></small>  2In + 3Li<small><sub>2</sub></small>S</span></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(1)</td></tr></tbody></table><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn2"><span id="eqn2">3In + 13Li<small><sup>+</sup></small> + 13e<small><sup></sup></small>  In<small><sub>3</sub></small>Li<small><sub>13</sub></small></span></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(2)</td></tr></tbody></table></span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig5"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f5_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f5.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f5.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 5 </b> <span id="fig5"><span class="graphic_title">Electrochemical performances and <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD pattern of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode in LIBs. (a) CV curves at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, (b) <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD pattern, (c) rate performance at 502000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, and (d and e) cycling performance at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">To sum up, the lithium storage mechanism of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> could be elucidated as <a title="" href="#eqn1">eqn (1) and (2)</a>. 14.67 moles of Li<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions and electrons are stored in one mole of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, and the maximum theoretical capacity of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> can be calculated to be 1206 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The electrochemical performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode was investigated by the galvanostatic discharge/charge test. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5c</a> shows the rate performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode at diverse current densities in the range of 502000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode experiences an obvious capacity decrease during the first several cycles, which is consistent with the CV test result. Fortunately, even at a high current density of 2000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode maintains a high discharge specific capacity of 301.2 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, and after the current density was restored to 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the specific capacity rapidly went back to 624.3 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The cycling performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and the corresponding first three discharge/charge profiles can be seen in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5d</a> and Fig. S6,<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> respectively. The initial discharge and charge specific capacities are 1184.2 and 696.4 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively, meaning that the initial coulombic efficiency is about 58.8%. The low reversibility of the conversion reaction and the irreversible formation of the SEI film are the main reasons for the 41.2% irreversible capacity loss.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit44"><sup><span class="sup_ref">44,45</span></sup></a> After 100 cycles, the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode delivered a high discharge specific capacity of 642.4 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> with a capacity retention of 95.1% (based on the second discharge specific capacity of 675.2 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>). Beyond that, the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode also shows ultra-long cycle life at 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5e</a>), maintaining a discharge specific capacity of 312.5 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 600 cycles with a capacity retention of 80.5% (based on the second discharge specific capacity of 388.3 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>). Compared with those of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> materials in published articles,<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit25"><sup><span class="sup_ref">25,46</span></sup></a> the electrochemical performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers in LIBs has been significantly improved. In the first several cycles, a minor specific capacity fade was observed at both 50 and 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. The capacity fade could be mainly ascribed to the low reversibility of the conversion reaction and the separation of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> floccules from the fiber framework, which will be explained in subsequent articles.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The electrode reaction kinetics was investigated by electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS). Fig. S8<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> shows the Nyquist plots, which include two depressed semicircles and a sloping line and the corresponding simulated curves of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode after 1 and 20 cycles at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Specifically, the high-frequency semicircle is related to the SEI film resistance as <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>sei</sub></small>, the semicircle in the intermediate-frequency region is related to the charge-transfer resistance as <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small>, and the sloping line is due to the ion-diffusion process in the solid phase.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit47"><sup><span class="sup_ref">47,48</span></sup></a> The simulated curves are obtained by constructing an equivalent circuit model (the inset in Fig. S8<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The simulated impedance parameters are listed in Table S1.<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode showed small impedance after 1 cycle and a negligible increase after 20 cycles. Moreover, the EIS of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode after 600 cycles at 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (corresponding to <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5e</a>) was also tested. After experiencing an ultra-long cycle, the continuous consumption of the electrolyte during repeated cycles leads to an increase of the <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>s</sub></small> value (25.9  after 600 cycles), which may be the reason why the specific capacity gradually decreases after 300 cycles. However, its <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value on behalf of the charge transfer resistance is still only 20.3 ; the small <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value indicates that the electrode structure of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode has not been destroyed after undergoing an ultra-long cycle. The small <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value benefits mainly from the carbon matrix that fully encapsulates the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles and enhances their electrical conductivity.</p>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect664"><span class="b_heading">2.3 Sodium storage performance and sodium storage mechanism</span></h3>
        <span>The electrochemical performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers in SIBs was tested in Na half-cells. The electrochemical reaction mechanism of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> was investigated by CV and <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD analysis. The CV curves of the first three cycles can be seen in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6a</a>. In the first cathodic scan process, the two strong reduction peaks at 0.38 V and 0.54 V can be attributed to the conversion from In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> to In and Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S (<a title="" href="#eqn3">eqn (3)</a>) and the formation of the SEI film, respectively. The <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD pattern in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6b</a> confirms the formation of the orthorhombic Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S phase (the corresponding diffraction peak is located at 36.4) and tetragonal phase (after discharging to 0.4 V). The reduction peak below 0.2 V and the oxidation peak at 0.49 V in all cycles may be attributed to the InNa alloying reaction (<a title="" href="#eqn4">eqn (4)</a>) and the inverse dealloying reaction, respectively, which can also be confirmed by <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD results. A weak diffraction peak appeared at 21.0 when discharged to 0.01 V, which is absent when charged to 1.6 V; it could be assigned to the (1 1 1) plane of cubic NaIn. In addition, Fig. S5<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> shows the high-resolution In 3d spectrum at dis-0.01 V, which can be deconvoluted into three species. The peaks at 443.7 and 451.5 eV can be attributed to the metal indium.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit49"><sup><span class="sup_ref">49,50</span></sup></a> The metal indium peak shifted slightly to a lower binding energy, and two small peaks at 443.2 and 451.0 eV appeared, which may be due to the formation of NaIn, which caused the binding energy shift. Indium has less electronegativity than sodium, and it is easier for indium to obtain electrons. The density of the outer electron cloud increases and the shielding effect on the nucleus increases, thereby reducing the binding energy. During the charging process, the two peaks at 13.2 and 26.9 may be attributed to the (1 1 0) plane and the (2 2 1) plane of tetragonal Na<small><sub>8</sub></small>In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>7</sub></small> (4Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S + In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>  Na<small><sub>8</sub></small>In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>7</sub></small>), respectively. The intensity of the two peaks gradually disappears when the voltage increases to 2.5 V, which may be ascribed to the instability of Na<small><sub>8</sub></small>In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>7</sub></small> at high voltage, resulting in its decomposition. The formation of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> is a multi-step reversible conversion process corresponding to the oxidation peaks of 0.8 V and 1.2 V in the CV curve. When the voltage charges to 1.6 V, a diffraction peak reappears at 33.2 which can be attributed to the (0 0 12) plane of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>. In summary, 8 moles of electrons and Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> ions are stored in one mole of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>, indicating that the maximum theoretical capacity of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> can be calculated to be 658 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.<table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn3"><span id="eqn3">In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> + 6Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> + 6e<small><sup></sup></small>  2In + 3Na<small><sub>2</sub></small>S</span></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(3)</td></tr></tbody></table><table><tbody><tr><td class="leftEqn">&nbsp;</td></tr><tr><td class="eqn"><span id="eqn4"><span id="eqn4">2In + 2Na<small><sup>+</sup></small> + 2e<small><sup></sup></small>  2NaIn</span></span></td><td class="rightEqn">(4)</td></tr></tbody></table></span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig6"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f6_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f6.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f6.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 6 </b> <span id="fig6"><span class="graphic_title">Electrochemical performances and <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD pattern of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode in SIBs. (a) CV curves at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<small><sup>1</sup></small>, (b) <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD pattern, (c) rate performance at 502000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, and (d and e) cycling performance at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> and 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
        <p class="otherpara">In the subsequent CV scans, the shift of the reduction peak position may be put down to the phase transition and the formation of the SEI film.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit51"><sup><span class="sup_ref">51</span></sup></a> Beyond that, the CV curves overlap very well during the subsequent scans, indicating that the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode has high electrochemical reversibility.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The rate performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode was evaluated at diverse current densities in the range of 502000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6c</a>). The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode delivers a high specific capacity of 388.5 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Even if the applied current density increased to 2000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the capacity of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode can still be maintained at 235.6 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>. Then, the specific capacity quickly recovered to 344.7 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after the current density recovered to 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>.</p>
        <p class="otherpara">The cycle performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode in SIBs and the corresponding first three discharge/charge profiles were tested at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6d</a> and S7<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>). The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode delivers the first discharge and charge specific capacities of 683.6 and 393.7 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively, meaning that the initial coulombic efficiency is about 57.6%. The large first irreversible capacity fade is mainly to blame for the formation of the SEI film.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit11"><sup><span class="sup_ref">11,16</span></sup></a> After the initial few cycles, the coulombic efficiency was maintained close to 100%, manifesting that the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode has good stability and reversibility. The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode can maintain a high specific capacity of 372.4 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 100 cycles, and its capacity retention is 94.1% (based on the second discharge specific capacity of 395.9 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>). The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode also showed long-term cyclability (<a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">Fig. 6e</a>), which maintained a specific capacity of 261.7 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small> after 300 cycles at 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small> with a capacity retention of 97.3% (based on the second discharge specific capacity of 269.1 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>). The cycle life of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers in SIBs has been significantly increased compared with the published article in which the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> composite was used as an anode for SIBs.<a title="Select to navigate to references" href="#cit26"><sup><span class="sup_ref">26</span></sup></a></p>
        <p class="otherpara">The EIS was performed to investigate the electrode reaction kinetics of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode in SIBs. Fig. S9<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a> displays the Nyquist plots and corresponding simulated curves (simulated impendence parameters can be seen in Table S2<a title="Select to navigate to footnote" href="#fn1"></a>) of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode. The <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>s</sub></small> value is small with negligible increase. The addition of 5% FEC additive to the electrolyte of SIBs generated the formation of a compact SEI film on the surface of the electrode, which resulted in a large <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>sei</sub></small>, however, without significant increase after 20 cycles.<a title="Select to navigate to reference" href="#cit20"><sup><span class="sup_ref">20,52</span></sup></a> The large <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value is ascribed to the large sodium ion radius. Interestingly, there is no obvious increase in the <span class="italic">R</span><small><sub>ct</sub></small> value after 20 cycles, indicating a stable electrode structure in SIBs.</p>
      
      
        
        <h3 id="sect793"><span class="b_heading">2.4 Characterization of the after-cycled In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode</span></h3>
        <span>In order to clarify the reason why the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anodes have excellent electrochemical properties in LIBs and SIBs, the morphology and microstructure of the after-cycled In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode were observed by TEM and EDX elemental mapping. First, the Li half-cell and Na half-cell that have been subjected to the rate performance test (corresponding to <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig5">Fig. 5c</a> and <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig6">6c</a>) were disassembled, and then the electrolyte residue on the electrode surface was rinsed with dimethyl carbonate (DMC). Finally, the active materials coated on the copper foil were collected and dispersed by sonication in absolute alcohol. It can be seen in <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7a and f</a>, which show the TEM images of the after-cycled electrodes cycling in the Li half-cell and Na half-cell, that the after-cycled In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode retains the initial fibrous morphology after cycling at high current densities. <a title="Select to navigate to figure" href="#imgfig7">Fig. 7be and gj</a> show the EDX elemental mapping of the after-cycled electrodes cycling in the Li half-cell and Na half-cell. In the fiber region, all elements (C, In, S, and N) are evenly distributed without visible light spots, which is different from the elemental mapping of the pristine In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers. The disappearance of the light spots in the element mapping of In and S may be ascribed to the large volume expansion during the alloying reactions, which causes the separation of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> floccules from the fiber surface. No obvious elemental light spots implies that no agglomeration of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> occurs during the electrochemical reaction. These phenomena including the unbroken fiber structure, uniform element distribution, and no agglomeration manifest that the carbon fiber framework has robust mechanical flexibility to adequately protect the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> nanoparticles during repeated cycles.</span>
        <br><div class="image_table"><table><tbody><tr><td colspan="3" class="imgHolder" id="imgfig7"><a href="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f7_hi-res.gif" title="Select to open image in new window" onclick="open(this.href, &quot;_blank&quot;, &quot;toolbar=1,scrollbars=yes,resizable=1&quot;); return false;"><img alt="image file: d0nr04843g-f7.tif" src="/image/article/2020/NR/d0nr04843g/d0nr04843g-f7.gif"></a></td></tr><tr><td class="pushTitleRight"> </td><td class="image_title"><b>Fig. 7 </b> <span id="fig7"><span class="graphic_title">Characterization study of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode after the rate performance testing in LIBs: (a) TEM and (be) elemental mapping images. Characterization study of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode after the rate performance testing in SIBs: (f) TEM and (gj) EDX elemental mapping images.</span></span></td><td class="pushTitleLeft"> </td></tr></tbody></table></div>
      
    
    
      
      <h2 id="sect823"><span class="a_heading">3. Conclusions</span></h2>
      <span>In summary, a novel In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode material is synthesized by a simple method of electrospinning and subsequent heat treatment. The In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber anode exhibits excellent lithium/sodium storage properties such as high capacity, long-term cycle life, and outstanding rate performance. After 100 cycles at 50 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode shows a high capacity retention of 95.1% and 94.1% in LIBs and SIBs, respectively. Moreover, the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode exhibits a capacity retention of 80.5% (after 600 cycles) and 97.3% (after 300 cycles) in LIBs and SIBs at 1000 mA g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. The excellent electrochemical performance of the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers mainly benefits from the <span class="italic">in situ</span> carbon encapsulation, which not only greatly improves the conductivity of the composite but also buffers the volume expansion resulting from the alloying reaction. More than that, the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers with robust mechanical flexibility make the In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofiber electrode endure repeated cycles. Furthermore, the reaction mechanism of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in LIBs and SIBs has been illustrated with <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD. Based on the characterization result from the <span class="italic">ex situ</span> XRD test, the electrochemical reaction mechanism in both the LIBs and the SIBs includes the conversion reaction and the alloying reaction. The maximum theoretical specific capacities of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in LIBs and SIBs are calculated to be 1205 and 658 mA h g<small><sup>1</sup></small>, respectively. We believe that the clarified Li/Na storage mechanism can further stimulate the development of In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small> in the electrochemical energy storage field. In addition, the strategy of preparing In<small><sub>2</sub></small>S<small><sub>3</sub></small>/C nanofibers with electrospinning can also be applied to the preparation of other energy storage materials.</span>
